from sklearn.ensemble import RandomForestRegressor

# Refined Prime Gaps Model using RandomForest
rf_gap_model = RandomForestRegressor(n_estimators=100, random_state=42)
rf_gap_model.fit(X_gaps, y_gaps)

# Predict prime gaps with refined model
rf_predicted_gaps = rf_gap_model.predict(X_gaps)

plt.figure(figsize=(10, 6))
plt.plot(X_gaps, y_gaps, label='Observed Prime Gaps')
plt.plot(X_gaps, rf_predicted_gaps, label='Predicted Prime Gaps (RF)', linestyle='dashed')
plt.xlabel('Index')
plt.ylabel('Prime Gap')
plt.title('Observed and Predicted Prime Gaps (Refined Model)')
plt.legend()
plt.grid(True)
plt.show()

# Refined Residue Classes Model using RandomForest
rf_residue_model = RandomForestRegressor(n_estimators=100, random_state=42)
rf_residue_model.fit(X_residues, y_residues)

# Predict residue classes with refined model
rf_predicted_residues = rf_residue_model.predict(X_residues)

plt.figure(figsize=(10, 6))
plt.plot(X_residues, y_residues, label='Observed Residue Classes')
plt.plot(X_residues, rf_predicted_residues, label='Predicted Residue Classes (RF)', linestyle='dashed')
plt.xlabel('Index')
plt.ylabel('Residue Class')
plt.title('Observed and Predicted Residue Classes (Refined Model, mod 42)')
plt.legend()
plt.grid(True)
plt.show()

### Step 1: Geometric and Complex Analysis

#### Geometric Representation

Prime numbers exhibit interesting geometric properties. We can use these properties to model primes in the complex plane.

1. **Complex Plane Transformation:**
   - Transform prime numbers into the complex plane using a suitable function.
   - Analyze the resulting geometric patterns.

#### Implementation

```python
import numpy as np
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Transform primes into the complex plane
primes_complex = [complex(p, 0) for p in large_primes]

# Plot primes in the complex plane
plt.figure(figsize=(10, 6))
plt.scatter(np.real(primes_complex), np.imag(primes_complex), s=1, label='Primes')
plt.xlabel('Real Part')
plt.ylabel('Imaginary Part')
plt.title('Primes in the Complex Plane')
plt.legend()
plt.grid(True)
plt.show()
```

### Step 2: Modular Arithmetic and Symmetry

#### Symmetry and Residue Classes

1. **Symmetry Analysis:**
   - Analyze the symmetry properties of primes with respect to different moduli.
   - Identify patterns and regularities in residue classes.

#### Implementation

```python
# Symmetry analysis of residue classes
modulus = 42
residue_classes = [p % modulus for p in large_primes]

# Plot symmetry properties
plt.figure(figsize=(10, 6))
plt.hist(residue_classes, bins=range(modulus + 1), edgecolor='black')
plt.xlabel('Residue Class')
plt.ylabel('Frequency')
plt.title(f'Symmetry Analysis of Residue Classes (mod {modulus})')
plt.grid(True)
plt.show()
```

### Step 3: Advanced Predictive Techniques

#### Machine Learning Models

1. **Feature Engineering:**
   - Create features based on geometric and modular properties.
   - Use these features to train machine learning models.

2. **Model Training:**
   - Train advanced models such as neural networks or ensemble methods to predict primes.
   - Evaluate model performance and refine predictions.

#### Implementation

```python
from sklearn.neural_network import MLPClassifier

# Feature engineering: create features based on primes
X_features = np.array([[p, p % modulus] for p in large_primes])
y_labels = np.array([1] * len(large_primes))

# Train a neural network model to predict primes
nn_model = MLPClassifier(hidden_layer_sizes=(100,), max_iter=1000, random_state=42)
nn_model.fit(X_features, y_labels)

# Evaluate model performance
predicted_labels = nn_model.predict(X_features)
accuracy = np.mean(predicted_labels == y_labels)
print(f'Model Accuracy: {accuracy}')
```

import numpy as np
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Generate a larger dataset of primes
large_primes = list(sp.primerange(0, 100000))

# Transform primes into the complex plane
primes_complex = [complex(p, 0) for p in large_primes]

plt.title('Primes in the Complex Plane')

### Step 2: Modular Arithmetic and Symmetry

# Symmetry analysis of residue classes
modulus = 42

### Step 3: Advanced Predictive Techniques

Incorporate machine learning techniques to build predictive models for prime distributions.

#### Machine Learning Models

1. **Feature Engineering:**
   - Create features based on geometric and modular properties.

2. **Model Training:**
   - Train advanced models such as neural networks to predict primes.

```python
from sklearn.neural_network import MLPClassifier
from sklearn.model_selection import train_test_split
from sklearn.metrics import accuracy_score

# Feature engineering: create features based on primes
X_features = np.array([[p, p % modulus] for p in large_primes])
y_labels = np.array([1] * len(large_primes))

# Split the data into training and testing sets
X_train, X_test, y_train, y_test = train_test_split(X_features, y_labels, test_size=0.3, random_state=42)

# Train a neural network model to predict primes
nn_model = MLPClassifier(hidden_layer_sizes=(100,), max_iter=1000, random_state=42)
nn_model.fit(X_train, y_train)

# Evaluate model performance
predicted_labels = nn_model.predict(X_test)
accuracy = accuracy_score(y_test, predicted_labels)
print(f'Model Accuracy: {accuracy}')

# Plot the predicted results
plt.figure(figsize=(10, 6))
plt.scatter(X_test[:, 0], predicted_labels, s=1, label='Predicted Primes', alpha=0.6)
plt.scatter(X_test[:, 0], y_test, s=1, label='Actual Primes', alpha=0.6)
plt.xlabel('Prime Number')
plt.ylabel('Prediction')
plt.title('Predicted vs Actual Primes')
plt.legend()
plt.grid(True)
plt.show()
```

#### Advanced Geometric Analysis

1. **Apply Advanced Transformations:**
   - Use transformations such as the Möbius transformation or other complex functions.
   - Visualize and analyze the transformed primes.

#### Deepen Symmetry Analysis

1. **Explore Different Moduli:**
   - Analyze residue classes with various moduli and larger prime datasets.
   - Identify patterns and regularities in different modular settings.

1. **Feature Engineering:**
   - Create new features based on higher-order interactions and modular arithmetic properties.
   - Train and evaluate more sophisticated models.

### Example Implementation

```python
# Advanced Geometric Analysis: Apply Möbius transformation
def mobius_transform(z, a, b, c, d):
    return (a * z + b) / (c * z + d)

# Apply Möbius transformation to primes
a, b, c, d = 1, 1, 1, 1  # Example coefficients
transformed_primes = [mobius_transform(p, a, b, c, d) for p in primes_complex]

# Plot transformed primes
plt.figure(figsize=(10, 6))
plt.scatter(np.real(transformed_primes), np.imag(transformed_primes), s=1, label='Transformed Primes')
plt.xlabel('Real Part')
plt.ylabel('Imaginary Part')
plt.title('Primes Transformed by Möbius Transformation')
plt.legend()
plt.grid(True)
plt.show()

# Deepen Symmetry Analysis: Analyze residue classes with different moduli
moduli = [30, 36, 42, 48, 54]
for mod in moduli:
    residue_classes = [p % mod for p in large_primes]
    plt.figure(figsize=(10, 6))
    plt.hist(residue_classes, bins=range(mod + 1), edgecolor='black')
    plt.xlabel('Residue Class')
    plt.ylabel('Frequency')
    plt.title(f'Residue Class Distribution (mod {mod})')
    plt.grid(True)
    plt.show()

# Enhance Predictive Models: Feature engineering and model training
from sklearn.ensemble import RandomForestClassifier

# Create new features based on higher-order interactions and modular arithmetic properties
X_features_advanced = np.array([[p, p % mod, p // mod] for p in large_primes for mod in moduli])
y_labels_advanced = np.array([1] * len(large_primes) * len(moduli))

# Train an advanced model
rf_model = RandomForestClassifier(n_estimators=100, random_state=42)
rf_model.fit(X_features_advanced, y_labels_advanced)

# Evaluate model performance
predicted_labels_advanced = rf_model.predict(X_features_advanced)
accuracy_advanced = accuracy_score(y_labels_advanced, predicted_labels_advanced)
print(f'Advanced Model Accuracy: {accuracy_advanced}')
```

By implementing these steps, we can further refine our understanding of prime distributions and develop a comprehensive model to describe all primes.

### Assistant (2024-07-02 23:52:47)

# Advanced Geometric Analysis: Apply Möbius transformation
def mobius_transform(z, a, b, c, d):
    return (a * z + b) / (c * z + d)

# Apply Möbius transformation to primes
a, b, c, d = 1, 1, 1, 1  # Example coefficients
transformed_primes = [mobius_transform(p, a, b, c, d) for p in primes_complex]

# Plot transformed primes
plt.figure(figsize=(10, 6))
plt.scatter(np.real(transformed_primes), np.imag(transformed_primes), s=1, label='Transformed Primes')
plt.xlabel('Real Part')
plt.ylabel('Imaginary Part')
plt.title('Primes Transformed by Möbius Transformation')
plt.legend()
plt.grid(True)
plt.show()

# Deepen Symmetry Analysis: Analyze residue classes with different moduli
moduli = [30, 36, 42, 48, 54]
for mod in moduli:
    residue_classes = [p % mod for p in large_primes]
    plt.figure(figsize=(10, 6))
    plt.hist(residue_classes, bins=range(mod + 1), edgecolor='black')
    plt.xlabel('Residue Class')
    plt.ylabel('Frequency')
    plt.title(f'Residue Class Distribution (mod {mod})')
    plt.grid(True)
    plt.show()

# Enhance Predictive Models: Feature engineering and model training
from sklearn.ensemble import RandomForestClassifier

# Create new features based on higher-order interactions and modular arithmetic properties
X_features_advanced = np.array([[p, p % mod, p // mod] for p in large_primes for mod in moduli])
y_labels_advanced = np.array([1] * len(large_primes) * len(moduli))

# Train an advanced model
rf_model = RandomForestClassifier(n_estimators=100, random_state=42)
rf_model.fit(X_features_advanced, y_labels_advanced)

# Evaluate model performance
predicted_labels_advanced = rf_model.predict(X_features_advanced)
accuracy_advanced = accuracy_score(y_labels_advanced, predicted_labels_advanced)
print(f'Advanced Model Accuracy: {accuracy_advanced}')

```python
# Geometric Transformations: Apply exponential map
def exponential_map(z):
    return np.exp(z)

# Apply exponential map to primes
exp_transformed_primes = [exponential_map(p) for p in primes_complex]

# Plot exponential map transformed primes
plt.figure(figsize=(10, 6))
plt.scatter(np.real(exp_transformed_primes), np.imag(exp_transformed_primes), s=1, label='Transformed Primes (Exponential Map)')
plt.xlabel('Real Part')
plt.ylabel('Imaginary Part')
plt.title('Primes Transformed by Exponential Map')
plt.legend()
plt.grid(True)
plt.show()

# Symmetry and Moduli Analysis: Expand moduli range
expanded_moduli = [60, 66, 72, 78, 84]
for mod in expanded_moduli:
    residue_classes = [p % mod for p in large_primes]
    plt.figure(figsize=(10, 6))
    plt.hist(residue_classes, bins=range(mod + 1), edgecolor='black')
    plt.xlabel('Residue Class')
    plt.ylabel('Frequency')
    plt.title(f'Residue Class Distribution (mod {mod})')
    plt.grid(True)
    plt.show()

# Model Refinement: Introduce more features and advanced models
from sklearn.ensemble import GradientBoostingClassifier

# Create new features based on prime gaps and higher-order residues
prime_gaps = [j - i for i, j in zip(large_primes[:-1], large_primes[1:])]
X_features_refined = np.array([[p, p % mod, p // mod, g] for p, g in zip(large_primes, prime_gaps) for mod in expanded_moduli])
y_labels_refined = np.array([1] * len(large_primes) * len(expanded_moduli))

# Train an advanced model with gradient boosting
gb_model = GradientBoostingClassifier(n_estimators=100, random_state=42)
gb_model.fit(X_features_refined, y_labels_refined)

# Evaluate model performance
predicted_labels_refined = gb_model.predict(X_features_refined)
accuracy_refined = accuracy_score(y_labels_refined, predicted_labels_refined)
print(f'Refined Model Accuracy: {accuracy_refined}')

### Implementation

#### Addressing Overflow Issues

1. **Geometric Transformations:**
   - Implement alternative transformations or scale inputs to prevent overflow.

#### Correcting Input Data Inconsistency

1. **Ensure Matching Dimensions:**
   - Verify that the feature and label arrays have consistent lengths.

### Example Implementation

```python
# Geometric Transformations: Handle overflow by scaling
def scaled_exponential_map(z, scale_factor=1e-5):
    return np.exp(z * scale_factor)

# Apply scaled exponential map to primes
scaled_transformed_primes = [scaled_exponential_map(p) for p in primes_complex]

# Plot scaled exponential map transformed primes
plt.figure(figsize=(10, 6))
plt.scatter(np.real(scaled_transformed_primes), np.imag(scaled_transformed_primes), s=1, label='Transformed Primes (Scaled Exponential Map)')
plt.xlabel('Real Part')
plt.ylabel('Imaginary Part')
plt.title('Primes Transformed by Scaled Exponential Map')
plt.legend()
plt.grid(True)
plt.show()

# Ensure matching dimensions for feature and label arrays
# Create new features based on prime gaps and higher-order residues
prime_gaps = [j - i for i, j in zip(large_primes[:-1], large_primes[1:])]
expanded_moduli = [60, 66, 72, 78, 84]
X_features_refined = []
y_labels_refined = []

for p, g in zip(large_primes, prime_gaps):
    for mod in expanded_moduli:
        X_features_refined.append([p, p % mod, p // mod, g])
        y_labels_refined.append(1)

X_features_refined = np.array(X_features_refined)
y_labels_refined = np.array(y_labels_refined)

# Train an advanced model with gradient boosting
gb_model = GradientBoostingClassifier(n_estimators=100, random_state=42)
gb_model.fit(X_features_refined, y_labels_refined)

# Evaluate model performance
predicted_labels_refined = gb_model.predict(X_features_refined)
accuracy_refined = accuracy_score(y_labels_refined, predicted_labels_refined)
print(f'Refined Model Accuracy: {accuracy_refined}')
```

By implementing these steps, we can address the overflow issues, correct the input data inconsistency, and refine our predictive models.

Let's proceed with these adjustments and re-train the advanced model.

### Assistant (2024-07-02 23:55:06)

### Analysis and Next Steps

#### Geometric Transformation

The scaled exponential map successfully transformed the primes without overflow issues, as shown in the plot. This approach can be further explored for other geometric transformations.

#### Model Training Error

The error indicates that the label array contains only one class, which is insufficient for training a classification model. This can be addressed by generating a balanced dataset with both prime and non-prime labels.

### Adjustments and Implementation

1. **Generate a Balanced Dataset:**
   - Include both prime and non-prime numbers in the dataset.
   - Ensure that the label array contains both classes.

2. **Feature Engineering:**
   - Create features for both prime and non-prime numbers.
   - Use the prime gaps and higher-order residues as features.

### Example Implementation

#### Generate a Balanced Dataset

1. **Include Non-Prime Numbers:**
   - Generate non-prime numbers and combine them with prime numbers.

2. **Create Features and Labels:**
   - Use prime gaps and higher-order residues as features.
   - Label primes as 1 and non-primes as 0.

```python
# Generate non-prime numbers
non_primes = [i for i in range(4, 100000) if not sp.isprime(i)]

# Combine primes and non-primes
combined_numbers = large_primes + non_primes

# Create prime gaps for combined numbers (excluding the first element)
combined_gaps = [j - i for i, j in zip(combined_numbers[:-1], combined_numbers[1:])]

# Create features and labels
X_features_balanced = []
y_labels_balanced = []

for p, g in zip(combined_numbers[:-1], combined_gaps):
    for mod in expanded_moduli:
        X_features_balanced.append([p, p % mod, p // mod, g])
        y_labels_balanced.append(1 if sp.isprime(p) else 0)

X_features_balanced = np.array(X_features_balanced)
y_labels_balanced = np.array(y_labels_balanced)

# Train an advanced model with gradient boosting
gb_model_balanced = GradientBoostingClassifier(n_estimators=100, random_state=42)
gb_model_balanced.fit(X_features_balanced, y_labels_balanced)

# Evaluate model performance
predicted_labels_balanced = gb_model_balanced.predict(X_features_balanced)
accuracy_balanced = accuracy_score(y_labels_balanced, predicted_labels_balanced)
print(f'Refined Model Accuracy (Balanced): {accuracy_balanced}')
```

By generating a balanced dataset and including both prime and non-prime labels, we can train and evaluate the refined model more effectively.

Let's proceed with these adjustments and re-train the advanced model.

import numpy as np
from sklearn.ensemble import GradientBoostingClassifier
from sklearn.linear_model import LogisticRegression
from sklearn.metrics import accuracy_score

# Reduce dataset size for initial training and testing
subset_size = 10000
subset_indices = np.random.choice(len(X_features_balanced), subset_size, replace=False)

X_features_subset = X_features_balanced[subset_indices]
y_labels_subset = y_labels_balanced[subset_indices]

# Train an advanced model with gradient boosting on the subset
gb_model_subset = GradientBoostingClassifier(n_estimators=100, random_state=42)
gb_model_subset.fit(X_features_subset, y_labels_subset)

# Evaluate model performance on the subset
predicted_labels_subset = gb_model_subset.predict(X_features_subset)
accuracy_subset = accuracy_score(y_labels_subset, predicted_labels_subset)
print(f'Gradient Boosting Model Accuracy (Subset): {accuracy_subset}')

# Optimize model parameters for full dataset
gb_model_optimized = GradientBoostingClassifier(n_estimators=50, learning_rate=0.1, random_state=42)
gb_model_optimized.fit(X_features_balanced, y_labels_balanced)

# Evaluate optimized model performance on full dataset
predicted_labels_optimized = gb_model_optimized.predict(X_features_balanced)
accuracy_optimized = accuracy_score(y_labels_balanced, predicted_labels_optimized)
print(f'Gradient Boosting Model Accuracy (Optimized): {accuracy_optimized}')

# Train a logistic regression model for faster training
lr_model = LogisticRegression(max_iter=1000, random_state=42)
lr_model.fit(X_features_balanced, y_labels_balanced)

# Evaluate logistic regression model performance
predicted_labels_lr = lr_model.predict(X_features_balanced)
accuracy_lr = accuracy_score(y_labels_balanced, predicted_labels_lr)
print(f'Logistic Regression Model Accuracy: {accuracy_lr}')

```python
# Create additional features based on higher-order interactions and number theory properties
def create_features(numbers, gaps, moduli):
    features = []
    for p, g in zip(numbers, gaps):
        for mod in moduli:
            features.append([p, p % mod, p // mod, g, (p ** 2) % mod, (p ** 3) % mod])
    return np.array(features)

# Generate features for combined numbers
expanded_moduli = [60, 66, 72, 78, 84]
X_features_expanded = create_features(combined_numbers[:-1], combined_gaps, expanded_moduli)
y_labels_expanded = np.array([1 if sp.isprime(p) else 0 for p in combined_numbers[:-1]])

# Train and evaluate an advanced model with the new features
gb_model_expanded = GradientBoostingClassifier(n_estimators=100, random_state=42)
gb_model_expanded.fit(X_features_expanded, y_labels_expanded)

# Evaluate model performance
predicted_labels_expanded = gb_model_expanded.predict(X_features_expanded)
accuracy_expanded = accuracy_score(y_labels_expanded, predicted_labels_expanded)
print(f'Gradient Boosting Model Accuracy (Expanded Features): {accuracy_expanded}')
```

### Assistant (2024-07-02 23:59:14)

The error indicates that the feature and label arrays have inconsistent lengths. This can be caused by an incorrect number of generated features or labels. Let's address this by ensuring the correct generation of features and labels.

### Adjustments and Implementation

1. **Correct Feature and Label Generation:**
   - Ensure that the number of features and labels match.

2. **Verify Data Consistency:**
   - Verify that each number has the correct set of features and corresponding label.

### Implementation

#### Correct Feature and Label Generation

1. **Ensure Matching Lengths:**
   - Generate features and labels with consistent lengths.

```python
# Correct feature and label generation
def create_balanced_features_labels(numbers, gaps, moduli):
    features = []
    labels = []
    for p, g in zip(numbers, gaps):
        for mod in moduli:
            features.append([p, p % mod, p // mod, g, (p ** 2) % mod, (p ** 3) % mod])
            labels.append(1 if sp.isprime(p) else 0)
    return np.array(features), np.array(labels)

# Generate features and labels for combined numbers
expanded_moduli = [60, 66, 72, 78, 84]
X_features_balanced, y_labels_balanced = create_balanced_features_labels(combined_numbers[:-1], combined_gaps, expanded_moduli)

# Verify lengths
print(f'Number of features: {len(X_features_balanced)}, Number of labels: {len(y_labels_balanced)}')

# Train and evaluate an advanced model with the new features
gb_model_balanced = GradientBoostingClassifier(n_estimators=100, random_state=42)
gb_model_balanced.fit(X_features_balanced, y_labels_balanced)

# Evaluate model performance
predicted_labels_balanced = gb_model_balanced.predict(X_features_balanced)
accuracy_balanced = accuracy_score(y_labels_balanced, predicted_labels_balanced)
accuracy_balanced
```

### Assistant (2024-07-03 00:00:56)

### Addressing Training Time Issue

The Gradient Boosting model is taking too long to train on the full dataset. To address this, let's proceed with a subset of the data for training and testing, as well as use logistic regression for faster training.

### Implementation

#### Train on Subset of Data

1. **Use a Smaller Subset:**
   - Select a smaller subset of the combined dataset for initial training and testing.

#### Example Implementation

```python
import numpy as np
from sklearn.ensemble import GradientBoostingClassifier
from sklearn.linear_model import LogisticRegression
from sklearn.metrics import accuracy_score

# Reduce dataset size for initial training and testing
subset_size = 50000
subset_indices = np.random.choice(len(X_features_balanced), subset_size, replace=False)

X_features_subset = X_features_balanced[subset_indices]
y_labels_subset = y_labels_balanced[subset_indices]

# Train an advanced model with gradient boosting on the subset
gb_model_subset = GradientBoostingClassifier(n_estimators=50, random_state=42)
gb_model_subset.fit(X_features_subset, y_labels_subset)

# Evaluate model performance on the subset
predicted_labels_subset = gb_model_subset.predict(X_features_subset)
accuracy_subset = accuracy_score(y_labels_subset, predicted_labels_subset)
print(f'Gradient Boosting Model Accuracy (Subset): {accuracy_subset}')

# Train a logistic regression model for faster training
lr_model = LogisticRegression(max_iter=1000, random_state=42)
lr_model.fit(X_features_subset, y_labels_subset)

# Evaluate logistic regression model performance
predicted_labels_lr = lr_model.predict(X_features_subset)
accuracy_lr = accuracy_score(y_labels_subset, predicted_labels_lr)
print(f'Logistic Regression Model Accuracy: {accuracy_lr}')
```

1. **Investigate Prime Gaps and Residue Classes:**
   - Analyze how the observed patterns in prime gaps and residue classes align with theoretical results.

### Example Implementation

```python
# Generate a larger dataset of primes and non-primes
large_primes = list(sp.primerange(0, 1000000))
non_primes_large = [i for i in range(4, 1000000) if not sp.isprime(i)]
combined_numbers_large = large_primes + non_primes_large

# Create prime gaps for combined numbers (excluding the first element)
combined_gaps_large = [j - i for i, j in zip(combined_numbers_large[:-1], combined_numbers_large[1:])]

# Generate features and labels for the larger dataset
expanded_moduli = [60, 66, 72, 78, 84]
X_features_large, y_labels_large = create_balanced_features_labels(combined_numbers_large[:-1], combined_gaps_large, expanded_moduli)

# Train and evaluate gradient boosting model on the larger dataset
gb_model_large = GradientBoostingClassifier(n_estimators=50, random_state=42)
gb_model_large.fit(X_features_large, y_labels_large)
predicted_labels_large = gb_model_large.predict(X_features_large)
accuracy_large = accuracy_score(y_labels_large, predicted_labels_large)
print(f'Gradient Boosting Model Accuracy (Large Dataset): {accuracy_large}')

# Train and evaluate logistic regression model on the larger dataset
lr_model_large = LogisticRegression(max_iter=1000, random_state=42)
lr_model_large.fit(X_features_large, y_labels_large)
predicted_labels_lr_large = lr_model_large.predict(X_features_large)
accuracy_lr_large = accuracy_score(y_labels_large, predicted_labels_lr_large)
print(f'Logistic Regression Model Accuracy (Large Dataset): {accuracy_lr_large}')

### Assistant (2024-07-03 00:04:07)

The current implementation attempt to train models on a larger dataset resulted in an error due to connection issues. To address this, we can split the process into smaller chunks and proceed with incremental steps to ensure stability.

### Adjustments and Implementation

1. **Split the Dataset:**
   - Split the large dataset into smaller manageable chunks.
   - Train and evaluate models incrementally.

2. **Combine Results:**
   - Aggregate results from smaller chunks to get overall performance metrics.

### Implementation

#### Split the Dataset into Chunks

1. **Split the Combined Dataset:**
   - Create smaller subsets for training and evaluation.

#### Example Implementation

```python
import numpy as np
from sklearn.ensemble import GradientBoostingClassifier
from sklearn.linear_model import LogisticRegression
from sklearn.metrics import accuracy_score

# Function to create features and labels in chunks
def create_balanced_features_labels_in_chunks(numbers, gaps, moduli, chunk_size):
    features = []
    labels = []
    for i in range(0, len(numbers), chunk_size):
        chunk_features, chunk_labels = create_balanced_features_labels(numbers[i:i+chunk_size], gaps[i:i+chunk_size], moduli)
        features.append(chunk_features)
        labels.append(chunk_labels)
    return np.vstack(features), np.hstack(labels)

# Create features and labels for combined numbers in chunks
chunk_size = 50000
X_features_chunks, y_labels_chunks = create_balanced_features_labels_in_chunks(combined_numbers_large[:-1], combined_gaps_large, expanded_moduli, chunk_size)

# Train and evaluate gradient boosting model on chunks
gb_model_large = GradientBoostingClassifier(n_estimators=50, random_state=42)
gb_model_large.fit(X_features_chunks, y_labels_chunks)
predicted_labels_large = gb_model_large.predict(X_features_chunks)
accuracy_large = accuracy_score(y_labels_chunks, predicted_labels_large)
print(f'Gradient Boosting Model Accuracy (Large Dataset, Chunks): {accuracy_large}')

# Train and evaluate logistic regression model on chunks
lr_model_large = LogisticRegression(max_iter=1000, random_state=42)
lr_model_large.fit(X_features_chunks, y_labels_chunks)
predicted_labels_lr_large = lr_model_large.predict(X_features_chunks)
accuracy_lr_large = accuracy_score(y_labels_chunks, predicted_labels_lr_large)
print(f'Logistic Regression Model Accuracy (Large Dataset, Chunks): {accuracy_lr_large}')
```

By splitting the large dataset into smaller chunks and aggregating results, we can ensure stability and efficiency in model training and evaluation.

Let's proceed with this approach to validate the models on a larger dataset.

### Assistant (2024-07-03 00:07:02)

import sympy as sp
import numpy as np
from sklearn.ensemble import GradientBoostingClassifier
from sklearn.linear_model import LogisticRegression
from sklearn.metrics import accuracy_score

# Regenerate the larger dataset of primes and non-primes
large_primes = list(sp.primerange(0, 1000000))
non_primes_large = [i for i in range(4, 1000000) if not sp.isprime(i)]
combined_numbers_large = large_primes + non_primes_large

# Create prime gaps for combined numbers (excluding the first element)
combined_gaps_large = [j - i for i, j in zip(combined_numbers_large[:-1], combined_numbers_large[1:])]

# Define the function to create balanced features and labels
def create_balanced_features_labels(numbers, gaps, moduli):
    features = []
    labels = []
    for p, g in zip(numbers, gaps):
        for mod in moduli:
            features.append([p, p % mod, p // mod, g, (p ** 2) % mod, (p ** 3) % mod])
            labels.append(1 if sp.isprime(p) else 0)
    return np.array(features), np.array(labels)

# Define the function to create features and labels in chunks
def create_balanced_features_labels_in_chunks(numbers, gaps, moduli, chunk_size):
    features = []
    labels = []
    for i in range(0, len(numbers), chunk_size):
        chunk_features, chunk_labels = create_balanced_features_labels(numbers[i:i+chunk_size], gaps[i:i+chunk_size], moduli)
        features.append(chunk_features)
        labels.append(chunk_labels)
    return np.vstack(features), np.hstack(labels)

# Create features and labels for combined numbers in chunks
expanded_moduli = [60, 66, 72, 78, 84]
chunk_size = 50000
X_features_chunks, y_labels_chunks = create_balanced_features_labels_in_chunks(combined_numbers_large[:-1], combined_gaps_large, expanded_moduli, chunk_size)

# Train and evaluate gradient boosting model on chunks
gb_model_large = GradientBoostingClassifier(n_estimators=50, random_state=42)
gb_model_large.fit(X_features_chunks, y_labels_chunks)
predicted_labels_large = gb_model_large.predict(X_features_chunks)
accuracy_large = accuracy_score(y_labels_chunks, predicted_labels_large)

### Assistant (2024-07-03 00:07:02)

The current implementation encountered an error due to the large size of the dataset and complexity. To address this, let's divide the dataset into smaller chunks and handle each chunk separately.

### Adjustments and Implementation

1. **Process Data in Smaller Chunks:**
   - Split the large dataset into smaller manageable chunks.
   - Train and evaluate models on each chunk separately.

2. **Combine Results:**
   - Aggregate results from the smaller chunks to get overall performance metrics.

### Implementation

#### Split the Dataset into Chunks

1. **Split the Combined Dataset:**
   - Create smaller subsets for training and evaluation.

### Example Implementation

```python
import sympy as sp
import numpy as np
from sklearn.ensemble import GradientBoostingClassifier
from sklearn.linear_model import LogisticRegression
from sklearn.metrics import accuracy_score

# Regenerate the larger dataset of primes and non-primes
large_primes = list(sp.primerange(0, 1000000))
non_primes_large = [i for i in range(4, 1000000) if not sp.isprime(i)]
combined_numbers_large = large_primes + non_primes_large

# Create prime gaps for combined numbers (excluding the first element)
combined_gaps_large = [j - i for i, j in zip(combined_numbers_large[:-1], combined_numbers_large[1:])]

# Define the function to create balanced features and labels
def create_balanced_features_labels(numbers, gaps, moduli):
    features = []
    labels = []
    for p, g in zip(numbers, gaps):
        for mod in moduli:
            features.append([p, p % mod, p // mod, g, (p ** 2) % mod, (p ** 3) % mod])
            labels.append(1 if sp.isprime(p) else 0)
    return np.array(features), np.array(labels)

# Define the function to create features and labels in chunks
def create_balanced_features_labels_in_chunks(numbers, gaps, moduli, chunk_size):
    features = []
    labels = []
    for i in range(0, len(numbers), chunk_size):
        chunk_features, chunk_labels = create_balanced_features_labels(numbers[i:i+chunk_size], gaps[i:i+chunk_size], moduli)
        features.append(chunk_features)
        labels.append(chunk_labels)
    return np.vstack(features), np.hstack(labels)

# Create features and labels for combined numbers in chunks
expanded_moduli = [60, 66, 72, 78, 84]
chunk_size = 50000
X_features_chunks, y_labels_chunks = create_balanced_features_labels_in_chunks(combined_numbers_large[:-1], combined_gaps_large, expanded_moduli, chunk_size)

# Train and evaluate gradient boosting model on chunks
gb_model_large = GradientBoostingClassifier(n_estimators=50, random_state=42)
gb_model_large.fit(X_features_chunks, y_labels_chunks)
predicted_labels_large = gb_model_large.predict(X_features_chunks)
accuracy_large = accuracy_score(y_labels_chunks, predicted_labels_large)
print(f'Gradient Boosting Model Accuracy (Large Dataset, Chunks): {accuracy_large}')

# Train and evaluate logistic regression model on chunks
lr_model_large = LogisticRegression(max_iter=1000, random_state=42)
lr_model_large.fit(X_features_chunks, y_labels_chunks)
predicted_labels_lr_large = lr_model_large.predict(X_features_chunks)
accuracy_lr_large = accuracy_score(y_labels_chunks, predicted_labels_lr_large)
print(f'Logistic Regression Model Accuracy (Large Dataset, Chunks): {accuracy_lr_large}')
```

By splitting the large dataset into smaller chunks and aggregating results, we can ensure stability and efficiency in model training and evaluation.

Let's proceed with this approach to validate the models on a larger dataset.

from sklearn.ensemble import GradientBoostingClassifier
from sklearn.linear_model import LogisticRegression

    labels = []

            features.append([p, p % mod, p // mod, g, (p ** 2) % mod, (p ** 3) % mod])
            labels.append(1 if sp.isprime(p) else 0)

    labels = []
    for i in range(0, len(numbers), chunk_size):
        chunk_features, chunk_labels = create_balanced_features_labels(numbers[i:i+chunk_size], gaps[i:i+chunk_size], moduli)
        features.append(chunk_features)
        labels.append(chunk_labels)
    return np.vstack(features), np.hstack(labels)

# Create features and labels for combined numbers in chunks
expanded_moduli = [60, 66, 72, 78, 84]
chunk_size = 50000
X_features_chunks, y_labels_chunks = create_balanced_features_labels_in_chunks(combined_numbers_large[:-1], combined_gaps_large, expanded_moduli, chunk_size)

# Train and evaluate gradient boosting model on chunks
gb_model_large = GradientBoostingClassifier(n_estimators=50, random_state=42)
gb_model_large.fit(X_features_chunks, y_labels_chunks)
predicted_labels_large = gb_model_large.predict(X_features_chunks)
accuracy_large = accuracy_score(y_labels_chunks, predicted_labels_large)
print(f'Gradient Boosting Model Accuracy (Large Dataset, Chunks): {accuracy_large}')

# Train and evaluate logistic regression model on chunks
lr_model_large = LogisticRegression(max_iter=1000, random_state=42)
lr_model_large.fit(X_features_chunks, y_labels_chunks)
predicted_labels_lr_large = lr_model_large.predict(X_features_chunks)
accuracy_lr_large = accuracy_score(y_labels_chunks, predicted_labels_lr_large)
print(f'Logistic Regression Model Accuracy (Large Dataset, Chunks): {accuracy_lr_large}')

### Tool (2024-07-03 00:13:42)

Encountered exception: <class 'websockets.exceptions.ConnectionClosedError'>.

### Assistant (2024-07-03 00:13:42)

It seems that running the entire process on the large dataset is causing connection issues. Let's break this down into even smaller steps to ensure stability.

### Adjusted Approach

1. **Split the Dataset into Chunks:**
   - Process each chunk individually.

2. **Train and Evaluate Models on Each Chunk:**
   - Train models on one chunk at a time to prevent overload.

3. **Combine Results:**
   - Aggregate results to get overall performance metrics.

### Example Implementation (Step-by-Step)

#### Split the Dataset into Chunks and Process Each Chunk

```python
import sympy as sp
import numpy as np
from sklearn.ensemble import GradientBoostingClassifier
from sklearn.linear_model import LogisticRegression
from sklearn.metrics import accuracy_score

# Regenerate the larger dataset of primes and non-primes
large_primes = list(sp.primerange(0, 1000000))
non_primes_large = [i for i in range(4, 1000000) if not sp.isprime(i)]
combined_numbers_large = large_primes + non_primes_large

# Create prime gaps for combined numbers (excluding the first element)
combined_gaps_large = [j - i for i, j in zip(combined_numbers_large[:-1], combined_numbers_large[1:])]

# Define the function to create balanced features and labels
def create_balanced_features_labels(numbers, gaps, moduli):
    features = []
    labels = []
    for p, g in zip(numbers, gaps):
        for mod in moduli:
            features.append([p, p % mod, p // mod, g, (p ** 2) % mod, (p ** 3) % mod])
            labels.append(1 if sp.isprime(p) else 0)
    return np.array(features), np.array(labels)

# Define the function to create features and labels in chunks
def process_chunk(numbers, gaps, moduli, start_idx, chunk_size):
    chunk_numbers = numbers[start_idx:start_idx + chunk_size]
    chunk_gaps = gaps[start_idx:start_idx + chunk_size]
    return create_balanced_features_labels(chunk_numbers, chunk_gaps, moduli)

# Parameters
expanded_moduli = [60, 66, 72, 78, 84]
chunk_size = 50000
total_chunks = len(combined_numbers_large) // chunk_size

# Initialize variables to store overall results
all_predicted_labels_gb = []
all_true_labels_gb = []
all_predicted_labels_lr = []
all_true_labels_lr = []

# Process each chunk
for chunk_idx in range(total_chunks):
    start_idx = chunk_idx * chunk_size
    X_features_chunk, y_labels_chunk = process_chunk(combined_numbers_large, combined_gaps_large, expanded_moduli, start_idx, chunk_size)
    
    # Train and evaluate gradient boosting model on the chunk
    gb_model = GradientBoostingClassifier(n_estimators=50, random_state=42)
    gb_model.fit(X_features_chunk, y_labels_chunk)
    predicted_labels_chunk_gb = gb_model.predict(X_features_chunk)
    
    # Train and evaluate logistic regression model on the chunk
    lr_model = LogisticRegression(max_iter=1000, random_state=42)
    lr_model.fit(X_features_chunk, y_labels_chunk)
    predicted_labels_chunk_lr = lr_model.predict(X_features_chunk)
    
    # Store results
    all_predicted_labels_gb.extend(predicted_labels_chunk_gb)
    all_true_labels_gb.extend(y_labels_chunk)
    all_predicted_labels_lr.extend(predicted_labels_chunk_lr)
    all_true_labels_lr.extend(y_labels_chunk)

# Calculate overall accuracy
accuracy_gb = accuracy_score(all_true_labels_gb, all_predicted_labels_gb)
accuracy_lr = accuracy_score(all_true_labels_lr, all_predicted_labels_lr)

print(f'Overall Gradient Boosting Model Accuracy: {accuracy_gb}')
print(f'Overall Logistic Regression Model Accuracy: {accuracy_lr}')
```

### Next Steps

1. **Validate Results:**
   - Check the results from each chunk and ensure consistency.

2. **Aggregate and Analyze:**
   - Aggregate results from all chunks to get overall performance metrics.

3. **Theoretical Connections:**
   - Investigate the theoretical implications of the model results.

Let's proceed with this incremental approach to ensure stability and validate the models on the larger dataset.

### Assistant (2024-07-03 00:16:13)

The error indicates that the dataset contains only one class after applying sample weights, which is insufficient for training the classification model. This can occur if the chunk being processed contains only prime or non-prime numbers.

### Adjustments

1. **Ensure Balanced Chunks:**
   - Ensure that each chunk contains a mix of both prime and non-prime numbers.

2. **Verify Data Balance:**
   - Check the balance of classes in each chunk before training the model.

### Implementation

#### Verify and Balance Chunks

1. **Check Class Distribution:**
   - Ensure each chunk has both classes before training.

### Example Implementation

```python
import sympy as sp
import numpy as np
from sklearn.ensemble import GradientBoostingClassifier
from sklearn.linear_model import LogisticRegression
from sklearn.metrics import accuracy_score

# Regenerate the larger dataset of primes and non-primes
large_primes = list(sp.primerange(0, 1000000))
non_primes_large = [i for i in range(4, 1000000) if not sp.isprime(i)]
combined_numbers_large = large_primes + non_primes_large

# Create prime gaps for combined numbers (excluding the first element)
combined_gaps_large = [j - i for i, j in zip(combined_numbers_large[:-1], combined_numbers_large[1:])]

# Define the function to create balanced features and labels
def create_balanced_features_labels(numbers, gaps, moduli):
    features = []
    labels = []
    for p, g in zip(numbers, gaps):
        for mod in moduli:
            features.append([p, p % mod, p // mod, g, (p ** 2) % mod, (p ** 3) % mod])
            labels.append(1 if sp.isprime(p) else 0)
    return np.array(features), np.array(labels)

# Define the function to create features and labels in chunks
def process_chunk(numbers, gaps, moduli, start_idx, chunk_size):
    chunk_numbers = numbers[start_idx:start_idx + chunk_size]
    chunk_gaps = gaps[start_idx:start_idx + chunk_size]
    return create_balanced_features_labels(chunk_numbers, chunk_gaps, moduli)

# Parameters
expanded_moduli = [60, 66, 72, 78, 84]
chunk_size = 50000
total_chunks = len(combined_numbers_large) // chunk_size

# Initialize variables to store overall results
all_predicted_labels_gb = []
all_true_labels_gb = []
all_predicted_labels_lr = []
all_true_labels_lr = []

# Process each chunk
for chunk_idx in range(total_chunks):
    start_idx = chunk_idx * chunk_size
    X_features_chunk, y_labels_chunk = process_chunk(combined_numbers_large, combined_gaps_large, expanded_moduli, start_idx, chunk_size)
    
    # Verify class balance
    unique_classes, class_counts = np.unique(y_labels_chunk, return_counts=True)
    if len(unique_classes) < 2:
        continue
    
    # Train and evaluate gradient boosting model on the chunk
    gb_model = GradientBoostingClassifier(n_estimators=50, random_state=42)
    gb_model.fit(X_features_chunk, y_labels_chunk)
    predicted_labels_chunk_gb = gb_model.predict(X_features_chunk)
    
    # Train and evaluate logistic regression model on the chunk
    lr_model = LogisticRegression(max_iter=1000, random_state=42)
    lr_model.fit(X_features_chunk, y_labels_chunk)
    predicted_labels_chunk_lr = lr_model.predict(X_features_chunk)
    
    # Store results
    all_predicted_labels_gb.extend(predicted_labels_chunk_gb)
    all_true_labels_gb.extend(y_labels_chunk)
    all_predicted_labels_lr.extend(predicted_labels_chunk_lr)
    all_true_labels_lr.extend(y_labels_chunk)

# Calculate overall accuracy
accuracy_gb = accuracy_score(all_true_labels_gb, all_predicted_labels_gb)
accuracy_lr = accuracy_score(all_true_labels_lr, all_predicted_labels_lr)

accuracy_gb, accuracy_lr
```

### Assistant (2024-07-03 14:06:24)

The process encountered an interruption due to long execution time. To handle this, we can further reduce the chunk size and focus on evaluating smaller portions of the dataset at a time.

### Adjusted Approach

1. **Reduce Chunk Size:**
   - Further reduce the chunk size to ensure each processing step completes within a reasonable time.

2. **Process and Aggregate:**
   - Train and evaluate models on smaller chunks and aggregate the results.

### Implementation

#### Split the Dataset into Smaller Chunks and Process Each Chunk

```python
import sympy as sp
import numpy as np
from sklearn.ensemble import GradientBoostingClassifier
from sklearn.linear_model import LogisticRegression
from sklearn.metrics import accuracy_score

# Regenerate the larger dataset of primes and non-primes
large_primes = list(sp.primerange(0, 1000000))
non_primes_large = [i for i in range(4, 1000000) if not sp.isprime(i)]
combined_numbers_large = large_primes + non_primes_large

# Create prime gaps for combined numbers (excluding the first element)
combined_gaps_large = [j - i for i, j in zip(combined_numbers_large[:-1], combined_numbers_large[1:])]

# Define the function to create balanced features and labels
def create_balanced_features_labels(numbers, gaps, moduli):
    features = []
    labels = []
    for p, g in zip(numbers, gaps):
        for mod in moduli:
            features.append([p, p % mod, p // mod, g, (p ** 2) % mod, (p ** 3) % mod])
            labels.append(1 if sp.isprime(p) else 0)
    return np.array(features), np.array(labels)

# Define the function to create features and labels in chunks
def process_chunk(numbers, gaps, moduli, start_idx, chunk_size):
    chunk_numbers = numbers[start_idx:start_idx + chunk_size]
    chunk_gaps = gaps[start_idx:start_idx + chunk_size]
    return create_balanced_features_labels(chunk_numbers, chunk_gaps, moduli)

# Parameters
expanded_moduli = [60, 66, 72, 78, 84]
chunk_size = 10000  # Reduced chunk size
total_chunks = len(combined_numbers_large) // chunk_size

# Initialize variables to store overall results
all_predicted_labels_gb = []
all_true_labels_gb = []
all_predicted_labels_lr = []
all_true_labels_lr = []

# Process each chunk
for chunk_idx in range(total_chunks):
    start_idx = chunk_idx * chunk_size
    X_features_chunk, y_labels_chunk = process_chunk(combined_numbers_large, combined_gaps_large, expanded_moduli, start_idx, chunk_size)
    
    # Verify class balance
    unique_classes, class_counts = np.unique(y_labels_chunk, return_counts=True)
    if len(unique_classes) < 2:
        continue
    
    # Train and evaluate gradient boosting model on the chunk
    gb_model = GradientBoostingClassifier(n_estimators=50, random_state=42)
    gb_model.fit(X_features_chunk, y_labels_chunk)
    predicted_labels_chunk_gb = gb_model.predict(X_features_chunk)
    
    # Train and evaluate logistic regression model on the chunk
    lr_model = LogisticRegression(max_iter=1000, random_state=42)
    lr_model.fit(X_features_chunk, y_labels_chunk)
    predicted_labels_chunk_lr = lr_model.predict(X_features_chunk)
    
    # Store results
    all_predicted_labels_gb.extend(predicted_labels_chunk_gb)
    all_true_labels_gb.extend(y_labels_chunk)
    all_predicted_labels_lr.extend(predicted_labels_chunk_lr)
    all_true_labels_lr.extend(y_labels_chunk)

# Calculate overall accuracy
accuracy_gb = accuracy_score(all_true_labels_gb, all_predicted_labels_gb)
accuracy_lr = accuracy_score(all_true_labels_lr, all_predicted_labels_lr)

accuracy_gb, accuracy_lr
```

Let's proceed with this adjusted approach to ensure stable and efficient processing.

### Example Implementation

```python
import sympy as sp
import numpy as np
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

# Generate a large dataset of primes
large_primes = list(sp.primerange(0, 1000000))

# Calculate prime gaps
prime_gaps = [j - i for i, j in zip(large_primes[:-1], large_primes[1:])]

# Plot the distribution of prime gaps
plt.figure(figsize=(10, 6))
plt.hist(prime_gaps, bins=range(1, 51), edgecolor='black', alpha=0.75)
plt.xlabel('Prime Gap')
plt.ylabel('Frequency')
plt.title('Distribution of Prime Gaps')
plt.grid(True)
plt.show()

# Analyze common prime gaps
unique_gaps, gap_counts = np.unique(prime_gaps, return_counts=True)
gap_distribution = dict(zip(unique_gaps, gap_counts))
print("Common Prime Gaps and Their Frequencies:", gap_distribution)
```

#### Step 2: Residue Class Distribution

1. **Calculate Residue Classes:**
   - Compute residue classes for primes modulo various numbers.

2. **Analyze Distribution:**
   - Plot and analyze the distribution of primes in different residue classes.

### Example Implementation

```python
# Define a modulus
modulus = 30

plt.grid(True)
plt.show()

residue_distribution = dict(zip(unique_residues, residue_counts

### Assistant (2024-07-03 14:11:26)

I understand the need to focus directly on the Riemann Hypothesis. Let's revisit and streamline our approach to address this objective directly.

### Steps to Address the Riemann Hypothesis

1. **Review the Hypothesis:**
   - The Riemann Hypothesis states that all non-trivial zeros of the Riemann zeta function \(\zeta(s)\) lie on the critical line \( \Re(s) = \frac{1}{2} \).

2. **Explore the Riemann Zeta Function:**
   - Analyze the properties of the Riemann zeta function and its zeros.
   - Investigate techniques used in previous attempts to prove or disprove the hypothesis.

3. **Mathematical and Computational Tools:**
   - Utilize both analytical methods and computational tools to explore the zeta function and its zeros.

### Step 1: Understanding the Riemann Zeta Function

The Riemann zeta function \(\zeta(s)\) is defined for \( \Re(s) > 1 \) by the series:
\[ \zeta(s) = \sum_{n=1}^{\infty} \frac{1}{n^s} \]
It can be analytically continued to other values of \(s\) except for a simple pole at \(s = 1\).

### Step 2: Properties of Zeros

1. **Trivial Zeros:** Zeros at negative even integers: \( s = -2, -4, -6, \ldots \)
2. **Non-trivial Zeros:** Conjectured to lie on the critical line \( \Re(s) = \frac{1}{2} \).

### Step 3: Analytical and Computational Methods

1. **Analytical Approach:**
   - Use properties of the zeta function and related functions (like the functional equation) to study zeros.
   - Examine critical points and regions.

2. **Computational Approach:**
   - Numerically compute zeros of the zeta function.
   - Validate computations against known results.

### Example Implementation

#### Analytical Exploration

Using properties and known results to analyze the zeta function.

```python
import sympy as sp

# Define the Riemann zeta function
s = sp.symbols('s')
zeta = sp.zeta(s)

# Functional equation for the zeta function
functional_equation = sp.Equality(sp.zeta(1 - s), 2**(1 - s) * sp.pi**(-s) * sp.sin(sp.pi * s / 2) * sp.gamma(s) * sp.zeta(s))

# Display the functional equation
functional_equation
```

#### Computational Exploration

Using numerical methods to find zeros on the critical line.

```python
import mpmath

# Function to compute zeta function values
def compute_zeta_zeros(num_zeros):
    zeros = mpmath.zetazero(num_zeros)
    return zeros

# Compute the first 10 zeros
zeros = compute_zeta_zeros(10)
zeros
```

   - Examine any emerging patterns and relate them to theoretical properties.

   - Explore advanced mathematical proof techniques (e.g., contour integration, complex analysis).
